  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_c76be807-28c6-4c88-8628-674d609f6c57'

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer17082985955132444474">Pemaknaan kembali kembali kopi, Buddha, Herman, surat tak tarkirimkan, cinta sejenis yang manis atau apa pun, membuktikan Dee tetap memesona. Kalau kemarin panitia Nobel sastra masih maju mundur dengan nama Pramoedya, sekarang bisa memaknai kembali, melalui karya-karya ini.<br/><br/>Ruang cerpen yang sempit dijadikannya wahana yang intens namun tidak sesak untuk mengungkapkan apa ya</span>
  <span id="freeText17082985955132444474" style="display:none">Pemaknaan kembali kembali kopi, Buddha, Herman, surat tak tarkirimkan, cinta sejenis yang manis atau apa pun, membuktikan Dee tetap memesona. Kalau kemarin panitia Nobel sastra masih maju mundur dengan nama Pramoedya, sekarang bisa memaknai kembali, melalui karya-karya ini.<br /><br />Ruang cerpen yang sempit dijadikannya wahana yang intens namun tidak sesak untuk mengungkapkan apa yang tak selalu mampu dikatakan. Lewat refleksi dan monolog interior yang digarap dengan cakap dan jernih. pembaca diajaknya menjelajahi halaman-halaman kecil dalam cerpen yang kini dijadikannya semesta kehidupan.<br /><br />Cerpen-cerpen Dee itu persis racikan kopi dari tangan seorang ahli peracik kopi: harum, menyegarkan, dan nikmat: pahit, tapi sekaligus mengandung manis. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17082985955132444474" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1412301917" />

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1412301917" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10948665204307586936"><i>Note: I’m writing this review in English because it’s the language I can comfortably express myself in however this book, unfortunately, is not available in English</i><br/><br/>This is a collection of short stories and prose. Her stories are full of life with a main focus on love. All kinds of love with all kinds of people who made their own life decisions, good or bad. There were many heartbreaking stories but there one particularly sweet one which I enjoyed. The one I really loved though is most interestin</span>
  <span id="freeText10948665204307586936" style="display:none"><i>Note: I’m writing this review in English because it’s the language I can comfortably express myself in however this book, unfortunately, is not available in English</i><br /><br />This is a collection of short stories and prose. Her stories are full of life with a main focus on love. All kinds of love with all kinds of people who made their own life decisions, good or bad. There were many heartbreaking stories but there one particularly sweet one which I enjoyed. The one I really loved though is most interestingly, the last story. A love story but… told from the perspective of a cockroach (<i>yea, Grooosss!</i>). He, however, is in love with a human girl (who’s absolutely frightened by cockroaches). I won’t say anymore about the story except that I found it a most beautiful story despite my prejudices against cockroaches.<br /><br />Because her book isn't available in English, I thought I’d translate one short prose for my English GR friends…<br /><br /><i><u>The Weather by Dee Lestari (1998)</u><br /><br />Talking about weather.<br /><br />To us, weather is a metaphor. Asking about weather is an expression we use when there is something else we wish to speak of.<br /><br />‘How’s your weather?’ ‘I’m blue.’ ‘I’m grey.’<br /><br />Pride split our path, the weather restrained us. Silence trapped us in doubt, a circular guessing game, where thoughts remain unspoken.<br /><br />‘How’s your weather?’<br />‘I’m sunny, not a cloud. You?’ ‘Bright and shiny. No cloud.’<br /><br />My soul flinched as I lied. His soul stuttered at being lied to. But, as one we have decided: to always be bright no matter what, for a cloudy sky means we do not belong together.<br /><br />As we lived through many weathers, the truth is swept further into a corner. Until one day, the storm will break, leaving only the truth to shine. Whether to strengthen or destroy…</i><br /><br />I’m hoping this isn't breaching any copyright… I've looked for a way to contact Dee Lestari to ask if I could share the above but I couldn't find one. If you know of one or if you know her, I’m happy to contact her or she can contact me to talk about this.<br /></span>

  <span id="freeText479565856985333151" style="display:none">To me this book is like a bible. I read it religiously, almost everyday. Especially at night when i can't sleep easily. About love and life. <br /><br />My fave stories are Spasi, Sikat gigi, and Surat yang tak pernah sampai.<br /><br />Here's my fave lines from Spasi:<br /><br />Napas akan melega dengan sepasang paru-paru yang tak dibagi. Jadi, jangan lumpuhkan aku dengan mengatasnamakan kasih sayang.<br /><br />Mari berkelana dengan rapat tapi tak dibebat. Janganlah saling membendung apabila tak ingin tersandung.<br /><br />Pegang tanganku, tapi jangan terlalu erat, karena aku ingin seiring dan bukan digiring.</span>

<div id="review_3257782672" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3257782672" />
    <a title="Missy J" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7406091-missy-j"><img alt="Missy J" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481102743p2/7406091.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3257782672?book_show_action=true">Apr 13, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Missy J" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Missy J" href="/user/show/7406091-missy-j">Missy J</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7406091-missy-j?shelf=asia-related">asia-related</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7406091-missy-j?shelf=read-in-indonesian">read-in-indonesian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7406091-missy-j?shelf=indonesia-related">indonesia-related</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7406091-missy-j?shelf=2020-books">2020-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7406091-missy-j?shelf=southeast-asia">southeast-asia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7406091-missy-j?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3257782672" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16891588054054594883">Dee Lestari is part of the Indonesian literature sub genre referred to as sastra wangi ("fragrant literature"). It's a label given at the turn of the 21st century to young and urban Indonesian women, who wrote openly about gender, sexuality, politics and religion. Ayu Utami's novel "Saman" is considered a quintessential example of sastra wangi. I am not sure if Laksmi Pamuntjak is part of this group, but I would believe it. So besides these two, I have always heard of Dee Lestari. "Filosofi Kopi</span>
  <span id="freeText16891588054054594883" style="display:none">Dee Lestari is part of the Indonesian literature sub genre referred to as sastra wangi ("fragrant literature"). It's a label given at the turn of the 21st century to young and urban Indonesian women, who wrote openly about gender, sexuality, politics and religion. Ayu Utami's novel "Saman" is considered a quintessential example of sastra wangi. I am not sure if Laksmi Pamuntjak is part of this group, but I would believe it. So besides these two, I have always heard of Dee Lestari. "Filosofi Kopi" was also turned into a cinematic experience, which was a hit. I haven't watched the movie, but I thought now is the right time to give this book and the author a try.<br /><br />"Filosofi Kopi" is the title of the first short story of this collection. It's one of the stronger stories, below you can read my short summaries and ratings of each of the 18 short stories. Overall, there were maybe 3 stories that I like a lot, but many left me feeling indifferent. Especially the one-page only short stories. Maybe a lot of the figurative meanings have escaped me due to the language, but I really couldn't understand the meaning or the point of some of the short stories. All in all, this short story collection is about love and the diversity of it. <br /><br />1. Filosofi Kopi (1996) (“Coffee philosophy”) about Ben, the coffee lover/expert/barista and Jody, his business partner. They run a coffee shop in Jakarta, which becomes very popular. Ben is very passionate about coffee. One day, a rich man challenges him to brew the most perfect coffee in the world. Ben brews and brews and finds the perfect recipe, only to learn an important lesson. *****<br />2. Mencari Herman (2004) (“Looking for Herman”) about Hera, the younger sister of the narrator’s best friend, who wants to meet a person named Herman in real life. Her life becomes a series of disappointments and tragedies in her search for this Herman. Once is enough, twice will kill. ***<br />3. Surat Yang Tak Pernah Sampai (2001) (“Letter that never arrived”) is a melodramatic description of a love that didn’t happen. *(*) <br /><i>"Tapi, hidup ini cair. Semesta ini bergerak. Realitas berubah. Seluruh simpul dari kesadaran kita berkembang mekar. Hidup akan mengikis apa saja yang memilih diam, memaksa kita untuk mengikuti arus agungnya yang jujur tetapi penuh rahasia. Kamu, tidak terkecuali."</i><br />4. Salju Gurun (1998) (“Snow desert”) advocates being different in the midst of uniformity. ***<br />5. Kunci Hati (1998) (“Heart’s key”) tells of the core of the heart and a person’s existence. *<br />6. Selagi Kau Lelap (2000) (“While you are asleep”) is a sentimental description of sleeping next to the one you love and making a mathematical formula out of love. *(*)<br />7. Sikat Gigi (1999) (“Toothbrush”) is about a couple with conflicting views on love. Tio thinks Egi is irrational and blind. She thinks he is too rational and blind too. To love, they have to compromise and go slow. **(*)<br />8. Jembatan Zaman (1998) (“The Bridge of Times”) believes that an older age doesn’t equal to more understanding and wisdom. There are different levels of understanding as we go through life. *(*)<br />9. Kuda Liar (1998) (“Wild Horse”) is about owning your freedom. That is love. *(*)<br />10. Sepotong Kue Kuning (1999) (“A Piece of Yellow Cake”) is the story of “the other woman.” Deep inside, Indi feels guilty for loving a married man. Their affair goes on for years and years. Indi must learn to value herself again. ***(*)<br />11. Diam (2000) (“Silent”) I did not get this. A couple in a room and both are silent. One of them is lying curled up and hugging him/herself. *<br />12. Cuaca (1998) (“Weather”) is a short description of speaking for the sake of it and not for the truth. *(*)<br />13. Lara Lana (2005) (“Lana’s pain”) is about a friendship between two people of different social classes. At first I thought Lana was a rich woman, but turns out it’s a man. It made me think whether it was about gay men? Or am I reading this completely wrong? **(*)<br />14. Lilin Merah (1998) (“Red Candle”) is a little piece about celebrating birthday in silence and about the candle on the birthday cake. *(*)<br />15. Spasi (1998) (“Space”) advocates for space in order to love. You don’t want to be repressed. ***<br />16. Cetak Biru (1998) (“Blueprint”) is a metaphor for realizing your dreams. Everybody has the blueprint of a house in side their head. Everybody’s house looks different. It’s our intention and heart that decides whether the house will be built. ***<br />17. Buddha Bar (2005) (“Buddha Bar”) is about Nelly who has 4 male friends. Each of the 4 men possesses a unique quality, so Nelly will never be able to pick one of them. **<br />18. Rico de Coro (1995) (“Rico de Coro”) is a hilarious story of a cockroach who is in love with a human being! *****<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16891588054054594883" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a title="Ernest Junius" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ernest Junius" href="/user/show/2978878-ernest-junius">Ernest Junius</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">lonely hearts</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Ernest by: </span>
      Amang
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2978878-ernest-junius?shelf=indonesian-books">indonesian-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2978878-ernest-junius?shelf=books-that-took-overnight-to-finish">books-that-took-overnight-to-finish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer81532926" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8695948773653494890">Reading from its title "Filosofi Kopi" ("The philosophy of Coffee") one might think that the book is filled with collections of exciting, epic stories that offer a fresh perspective about the popular roasted, brown seeds we know as coffee. <br/><br/>However to my dissapointment, the book is not all really about coffee. There is only one story that's associated with the book's title. The rest are merely love stories (and by saying this I don't mean to dislike the book).<br/><br/>The book in overall doesn't allure it</span>
  <span id="freeText8695948773653494890" style="display:none">Reading from its title "Filosofi Kopi" ("The philosophy of Coffee") one might think that the book is filled with collections of exciting, epic stories that offer a fresh perspective about the popular roasted, brown seeds we know as coffee. <br /><br />However to my dissapointment, the book is not all really about coffee. There is only one story that's associated with the book's title. The rest are merely love stories (and by saying this I don't mean to dislike the book).<br /><br />The book in overall doesn't allure its readers into a deep thought. It is just a series of simple, casual stories to read when you are whiling away. It doesn't require a lot of time nor a great amount of energy to finish the book, in my case, I was on the last page of the book in 90 minutes or so.<br /><br />Even though this book is one quick read, it doesn't sound kitschy. They are comprised of lots of little nuggets of inspiration and flicks of imagination that are really enjoyable. Some of the stories are good, but some are just barely even, however It's discernible to me that the author (Dee) really put exceptional efforts writing them. <br /><br />Lastly, agreeing with the title, the book to me is a sub for a cup of coffee. it accompanies a lonely heart on a cold, windy night, keeps you busy in the middle of a crowded cafe, it is also a great working companion and a great starter of the day as it is a loyal friend amidst of a wait.<br /><br />So I believe if you're looking for a book that talks great theories and philosophies about coffee, this is definitely not the book you're looking for, rather if you're simply looking for a cup of coffee and can't find one, I'm confident this book will do just fine. <br /><br />Thanks to Amang for lending me the book. I hope I can drop by the office this week to return the book!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8695948773653494890" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2793689678" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2793689678" />
    <a title="Sheany" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4451489-sheany"><img alt="Sheany" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1563193235p2/4451489.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2793689678?book_show_action=true">Apr 25, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sheany" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sheany" href="/user/show/4451489-sheany">Sheany</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2793689678" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1537961715454759816">I've always had a strange fascination for short stories, and the wonderment that comes with these little chapters in particular only furthered that fascination – I find myself so inspired with the incredible power that comes with only a few short pages. <br/><br/>I don't know where it first began, really, this strange... yearning, almost, to write as many words as possible. I guess it stemmed from those school exercises that emphasized more on the number of words rather than the actual value of your writt</span>
  <span id="freeText1537961715454759816" style="display:none">I've always had a strange fascination for short stories, and the wonderment that comes with these little chapters in particular only furthered that fascination – I find myself so inspired with the incredible power that comes with only a few short pages. <br /><br />I don't know where it first began, really, this strange... yearning, almost, to write as many words as possible. I guess it stemmed from those school exercises that emphasized more on the number of words rather than the actual value of your written work, though I suppose the prompt was meant to incorporate the two. But as a kid/teenager who knew so little about the world, writing with a specific amount of words can be a daunting task. That meant including a whole lot of bullshit, consisting of redundant arguments and repetitive words, in order to make that expected number of words. That sort of exercise, which you do through years of primary, middle and then high school, sticks around as a force of habit; even when you know it's not a great feature. <br /><br />These days, I try to focus less on the number of words and more on the quality of any essay, but quality also means information – and when there's an abundance of it, it's a tricky task to navigate your way through which ones to include or omit, and that's also something I'm still learning to accomplish. <br /><br />Don't think that all that didn't have a thing to do with the book – it does. It's what makes these stories even more precious, the way that they are so simply narrated, and at times without fuss, just straight to the main idea, but still very heartfelt and even poetic. That could be extra challenging in Indonesian, mind you, where redundancies pretty much makes the chunk of our exchanges (or at least that seems to be the case in my own humble opinion). <br /><br />It's hard to pick a favourite, really, because every chapter was a gem in itself. The story of Herman makes me wonder about the things we look for in life and the choices we make in life, whereas the tale about the toothbrush reminds me of hope in love. There's also the story of Rico, which prompts me to think about life in a magnified way; sadly not as easy as it sounds in a world filled with skepticism and ridicule over so many things that are actually valuable, though perhaps not right away. <br /><br />Thank you to my dear Sarah for gifting me this one, as it once again reminds me of how much in Indonesian literature there are for me to enjoy and learn from, as well as the joys of reading in Indonesian. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1537961715454759816" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3871500194516490924">I only love one part "Spasi" (1998). Didn't really attached with the rest and didn't find it relevant, tbh.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4565834180175565721">My first book of Dee... and I'm quite disappointed. I've seen adaptations of her books and had much more fun than from this.<br/><br/>The book is imho too cerebral. A little of action, too much thinking/thoughts of characters/making up things what somebody else might be doing. The action gets watery between the long descriptions and a bit of dialogues.   <span id="freeText4565834180175565721" style="display:none">My first book of Dee... and I'm quite disappointed. I've seen adaptations of her books and had much more fun than from this.<br /><br />The book is imho too cerebral. A little of action, too much thinking/thoughts of characters/making up things what somebody else might be doing. The action gets watery between the long descriptions and a bit of dialogues. I'm not a fan of long descriptions/thinking. <br /><br />The book contains 18 stories, without any order. At least not chronological. Maybe it was explained in introduction, haven't read it. ;) Some of the stories are really short, just 2 pages long. Some are unfortunately too long. (Mencari Herman - Looking for Herman).<br /><br />The funniest story was... surprisingly the last one - "Rico de Coro". I hate cockroaches, I'm scared of them like Sarah... but it was probably the lightest and funniest story. I still hate cockroaches. :D <br /><br />I'm relieved I've finished it. I was rather forcing myself to finish it. <br /><br />The ** is because it had some good moments. It's not exactly "didn't like it". Some of the stories are nice. It's probably just "too much of it". The book is not my style, but generally not bad. It's ok = it's not that bad.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17434528-nisa?shelf=compilations">compilations</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer535026374" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8346384976763513205">This is the second book by Dee that I've read, the first being Rectoverso. And unlike Rectoverso, which amuses me but doesn't tug any of my skeptical heartstrings, this book actually.. touches me.<br/><br/>It touches me in a way that was so familiar. It describes feelings so mundane in ways I've never thought of before. And some of the paragraphs are just so intense, I had to put the little brown book on my lap and close my eyes for a moment before continuing reading. And it hits oh-so-close to the bone. </span>
  <span id="freeText8346384976763513205" style="display:none">This is the second book by Dee that I've read, the first being Rectoverso. And unlike Rectoverso, which amuses me but doesn't tug any of my skeptical heartstrings, this book actually.. touches me.<br /><br />It touches me in a way that was so familiar. It describes feelings so mundane in ways I've never thought of before. And some of the paragraphs are just so intense, I had to put the little brown book on my lap and close my eyes for a moment before continuing reading. And it hits oh-so-close to the bone. Like a pair of gloves that fits my hands snugly. (Oh, the one about the unsent letters...)<br /><br />Another plus point: The language was not 'literature-ish' in that heavy, difficult kind of way, but it was clear and well-written. I'm thinking of continuing my Dee with her 'Supernova' saga, but I don't know yet if I have the determination...</span>

          </span>

Like a pair of gloves that fits my hands snugly. (Oh, the one about the unsent letters...)<br /><br />Another plus point: The language was not 'literature-ish' in that heavy, difficult kind of way, but it was clear and well-written. I'm thinking of continuing my Dee with her 'Supernova' saga, but I don't know yet if I have the determination...</span>
  <a data-text-id="7989006612362076402" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Coffee has been my personal dopping and nothing can replace it if i have to survive night to work on my assignment.<br /><br />I always fall in love with Dee's works on giving little details that made the characters alive. She doesn't really try to be a smart-ass but rather she reminds us of the feeling we often repressed. Her works are easy to read but at the same time compel you to contemplate and make you ask to your heart : How do i really feel under this circumstances?<br /><br />Her works are just soooo effortless! </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Wx+d1ErUQLA3fNTg/Oj+HHzY0ptxBV6FP/9qfdmZ2WDe00m7gQx16VUfEPl5gjEnjStR5rLgPKsWjqGjwewVug==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('TTW6AJTzQJVefccLRh6BTWCWQVoY0t65rlBJEJW3AQLI+W5vXyt1zDweAxLDdE52kWXCJ9s3vJeHIYLOjcLN2A==')})
  }

</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/164478.Dee_Lestari">About Dee Lestari</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/164478.Dee_Lestari"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1185996159p3/164478.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/164478.Dee_Lestari">Dee Lestari
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer16197506940283517464">Dee Lestari, is one of the bestselling and critically acclaimed writers in Indonesia.<br/>Born in January 20, 1976, she began her debut with a serial novel: Supernova in 2001. Supernova’s first episode, <i>Kesatria, Putri, dan Bintang Jatuh</i> (The Knight, The Princess, and The Falling Star), was sold phenomenally, achieving a cult status among Indonesian young readers. She has published four other episodes:</span>
  <span id="freeText16197506940283517464" style="display:none">Dee Lestari, is one of the bestselling and critically acclaimed writers in Indonesia.<br />Born in January 20, 1976, she began her debut with a serial novel: Supernova in 2001. Supernova’s first episode, <i>Kesatria, Putri, dan Bintang Jatuh</i> (The Knight, The Princess, and The Falling Star), was sold phenomenally, achieving a cult status among Indonesian young readers. She has published four other episodes: <i>Akar</i> (The Root), <i>Petir</i> (The Lightning), <i>Partikel</i>(The Particle), and <i>Gelombang</i> (The Wave). <br />Aside of the Supernova series, Dee has also published a novel titled <i>Perahu Kertas</i> (Paper Boat), and three anthologies: <i>Filosofi Kopi</i> (Coffee’s Philosophy), <i>Madre</i>, and <i>Rectoverso</i> — a unique hybrid of music and literature. <br />Dee also has an extensive music career, producing four albums with her former vocal trio, and two solo albums. She has been writing songs for renowned Indonesian artists. <br /><i>Perahu Kertas</i> (Paper Boat) was turned into a movie in 2009, marking Dee’s debut as a screenplay writer. The movie became one of the national's block busters. Following the same path, <i>Madre, Filosofi Kopi, Madre,</i> and <i>Supernova KPBJ,</i> were made into movies. <br />In February 2016, Dee released the final episode of Supernova, <i>Inteligensi Embun Pagi</i> (Intelligence of the Morning Dew). All Dee’s books are published by Bentang Pustaka. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16197506940283517464" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
